8d:["$","ol",null,{"children":["\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"In SQD, a quantum computer generate samples and a classical computer projects a Hamiltonian onto a subspace spanned by the samples and diagonalizes it to compute eigenvalues and eigenvectors.","className":"my-12"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"The generated samples should be from the target (ground) state support.","className":"my-12"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"Depending on the problem, the quantum state preparation and sample generation flow can be iterative or non-iterative.","className":"my-12"}],"\n",["$","li",null,{"children":"SQD works best for sparse wave functions. 14f:["$","td",null,{"align":"left","children":"In SQD, we do not need different measurement circuits for each grouped Pauli terms. Typically, we measure a single circuit for a fixed number of shots.
